GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4238

THE CONSTITUTION OF KENYA

APPOINTMENT

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by Article 132 (2) ( e )  of the Constitution, I, William Samoei Ruto, President of the Republic of Kenya and Commander-in-Chief of the Defence Forces, appoint-

KOSIOM FRANK OLE KIBELEKENYA

as  an  Ambassador  within  the  Foreign  Service  of  the  Republic  of Kenya.

Dated the 23rd March, 2026.

WILLIAM SAMOEI RUTO,

President .

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4239

EXECUTIVE OFFICE OF THE PRESIDENT

THE NATIONAL ECONOMIC AND SOCIAL COUNCIL AMENDMENT

PURSUANT  to  Gazette  Notice  No.  7699  of  2004,  I,  William Samoei Ruto, President of the Republic of Kenya and Commander-inChief of the Defence Forces, amends the said Gazette Notice:

(a) In paragraph (1)

(i) By deleting the introductory portion thereto and substituting therefor the following -

The  National  Economic  and  Social  Council  will  be chaired  by  the  President,  or  in  the  absence  of  the President, by the Prime Cabinet Secretary who shall be the convenor of the Council meetings, or in the absence of both the representative from  the private sector appointed by the President.

The Council shall comprise of the following:

(i) By deleting paragraph (b) and substituting therefor the following-

(b) The Prime Cabinet Secretary

(ii) By  inserting  the  following  sub-paragraphs  immediately  after sub-paragraph (b)

(ba)  The  Prime  Cabinet  Secretary  -  First  Vice-Chairperson and Convenor

(bb)  A representative from the private sector.

(bc) The  Cabinet  Secretaries  responsible  for  matters  relating to; -

(i) Foreign Affairs;

(ii) The National Treasury;

(iii) Education;

(viii) Investments, Trade and Industry;

(ii) By deleting paragraph (d) and substituting therefor the following-

Up to fifteen (15) Members, comprising local and international  experts.  All  experts  shall  be  of  the  highest repute, with demonstrably distinguished careers in business, economics, engineering and other sciences, public service,  administration  and  planning  or  civil  society,  and drawn from diverse professional and disciplinary backgrounds;

Cabinet Secretaries for the National Treasury and Economic  Planning;  Foreign  Affairs;  Investment,  Trade and Industry and Education  shall serve as Ex-Officio members.

Other  Cabinet  Secretaries  and  Principal  Secretaries  may attend,  as  directed  by  His  Excellency  the  President,  when their participation is deemed necessary for effective deliberations of the subjects under the agenda;

(iii) By deleting paragraph (f)

(iv) By deleting paragraph (h)

(v) By deleting paragraph (i)

2. By deleting sub-paragraph ( a ) to ( g ) and substituting therefor the following;

(a) To  advise  His  Excellency  the  President  and  the  Cabinet  on economic and social policy, including the articulation of longterm  goals  and  the  identification  of  appropriate  strategies  for their attainment;

(b) To  propose  a  long-term  national  development  framework, Vision Centenary, that transforms present challenges into building  blocks  toward  the  nation's  long-term  goals,  thereby positioning Kenya for inclusive development, shared prosperity, and a legacy worthy of its centenary of independence;

(c) To deliberate with originality, ingenuity, and foresight, and to propose  innovative  initiatives  across  strategic  sectors  vital  to national  development  and  wealth  creation,  including  energy, water,  health,  education,  infrastructure,  industry,  agriculture and digital technology;

(d) To  advise on social and governance  priorities, including addressing joblessness particularly providing decent jobs among young Kenyans, eradicating corruption, reducing inequalities  between  the  rich  and  the  poor  as  well  as  across regions, and empowering marginalized communities;

(e) To  advise  on  debt  management  and  resource  mobilization through innovative financing strategies;

(f) To  advise  on  the  blue  economy,  climate  change  and  green growth, sustainable management of natural resources, and the protection of wildlife; in accordance with Kenya's constitutional obligation to protect the environment for present and future generations; and

(g) To render such advice, opinions, and recommendations on any other matter of an economic or social nature referred to it by the President, the Cabinet, or Parliament.

 By  inserting  the  following  paragraphs  3  (d)  immediately  after subparagraph (c) the following:

(d) Shall prepare, publish and publicize bi-annual reports.

(e)  Subject to existing laws, the Council shall have access to such data  and  information  as  may  be  necessary  to  perform  its function.

By deleting Paragraph (4(1)) and substituting therefor the following -

The Secretariat of the Council shall be based at the Office of the Prime  Cabinet  Secretary,  P.O.  Box  30551-00100,  Nairobi  and  shall consist of: -

( a )   a  Secretary appointed by the President who shall be the Chief Executive Officer of the Council, responsible to the Council in carrying out the functions set out in paragraph (2); and

( b ) such other divisions of the Secretariat as may be found to be necessary for the performance of its functions, which shall be under the supervision of the Chief Executive Officer; and

( c )   such other officers, staff or agents as may be necessary for the discharge of the functions and duties of the Secretariat.

By inserting Paragraph 4 the following-

The funds necessary for the implementation of activities by the Council and the Secretariat, shall be appropriated and may also raise funds from any other sources.

Dated the 23rd March, 2026.

WILLIAM SAMOEI RUTO,

President.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4240

THE COUNTY GOVERNMENTS ADDITIONAL ALLOCATIONS (NO. 2) ACT

(No. 28 of 2025 )

CASH DISBURSEMENT SCHEDULE FOR THE KENYA URBAN SUPPORT PROGRAMME PHASE TWO - URBAN DEVELOPMENT GRANT CONDITIONAL ALLOCATIONS TO COUNTY GOVERNMENTS FOR FINANCIAL YEAR 2025/2026

IT  IS  notified  for  the  general  information  of  the  public  that pursuant  to  section  6  (2)  ( m )  and  ( o )  of  the  County  Governments

Additional Allocations (No. 2) Act, 2025, that the conditional additional  allocations  financed  from  proceeds  from  the  International Development Association - World Bank Credit to finance the Kenya Urban Support Programme Phase Two - Urban Development Grant, have  been  allocated to  the  beneficiary  county  governments  and respective municipalities specified in  column  A  and  column  B respectively, in the amounts specified in column C and column D of the Schedule hereto and revokes the conditional additional allocations financed from proceeds from the International Development Association - World Bank Credit to finance the Kenya Urban Support Programme Phase Two - Urban Development Grant in Gazette Notice number 1442 of 2026.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4256

THE LAND ACT

(Cap. 280 )

WAIVER OF INTEREST AND PENALTIES ON OUTSTANDING LOANS IN SETTLEMENT SCHEMES

IT  IS  notified  for  the  general  information  of  the  public  that  the Land  Settlement  Fund  Board  of  Trustees,  established  under  sections 134 and 135 of the Land Act, 2012, administers the Land Settlement Fund for purposes of implementing settlement schemes in the Republic of Kenya.

Settlement schemes are implemented by the National Government in consultation with the National Land Commission and the respective county governments.

Settlement  schemes  play  an  important  role  in  supporting  land access, agricultural  production  and  rural  development  in  Kenya. Currently, there are five hundred and twenty (520) settlement schemes across twenty-six (26) counties, of which four hundred and eighty-four (484) are registered and thirty-six (36) are undergoing registration.

It is further notified that the Cabinet, has approved a waiver of all outstanding  interest  and  penalties  on  land  and  development  loans issued under the Land Settlement Fund.

Accordingly-

(a) all  outstanding  interest  and  penalties  on  loans  issued  under the Land Settlement Fund are waived;

(b) a moratorium period of twelve (12) months, commencing on 13th February 2026, is granted to all settlers and individual plot  owners  to  pay  the  outstanding  principal  loan  amount only;

(c) all settlers with  outstanding  principal loan balances  are required to utilise the moratorium  period to settle the principal amount due; and

(d) upon the expiry of the moratorium period on 14th February 2027,  any  unpaid  principal  amount  shall  attract  interest  in accordance with the applicable terms of the Land Settlement Fund loans.

Settlers and plot owners may obtain their individual principal loan balances by accessing the official website of the Ministry at www.lands.go.ke and following the prescribed guidelines.

ALICE WAHOME, Cabinet Secretary for Lands. Public, Works Housing & Urban Development.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4260

THE MINING ACT

( Cap . 306)

THE MINING (AWARD OF MINERAL RIGHTS BY TENDER) REGULATIONS

( L.N. 153 of 2017)

TENDER NOTICE

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by regulation 6 (1) ( a ) of the  Mining  (Award  of  Mineral  Rights  by  Tender)  Regulations,  2017 the Cabinet Secretary for Mining, Blue Economy and Maritime Affairs advertises the following tender: -

REQUEST FOR EXPRESSION OF INTEREST FOR LARGE SCALE MINERAL RIGHTS OF COPPER AT KAMACABI IN THARAKA NITHI COUNTY, KENYA

Project Background

The Government of Kenya, through the Ministry of Mining, Blue Economy,  and  Maritime  Affairs,  has  designated  several  minerals  as Strategic  Minerals.  Copper  is  one  of  these  minerals  categorised  as strategic.  To  commercialize  this  resource,  the  government  plans  to award  mineral  rights  in  the  area  via  a  public  tender  process,  in accordance with the Mining Act (Cap. 306) and the Mining (Award of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017.

Upon  issuance  of  the  Mineral  Right  (Prospecting  Licence),  the project proponent will be expected to adhere to the provisions of the Mining Act and its attendant regulations.

Project Overview

The metamorphic rocks of the area formed in the Neoproterozoic era  with  mineralogical  composition  resulting  from  regional  plastic deformation and granitization from pre-existing sedimentary rocks of highly  varying  classes.  Varieties  of  gabbros,  norites,  bojites  and pyroxenites and their derivatives form the bulk of the basic intrusive rocks documented in the area. The chemical and mineralogical profiles of  the  basic-ultrabasic  rocks  are  highly  varied  with  hypersthene, olivine,  plagioclase  and  hornblende  generally  being  the  dominant constituent  minerals.  Hornblendite,  pyroxenite,  peridotites,  dolerites and diorites have been documented  as  common  basic  intrusive associated  with  the  metamorphic  rocks.  Both  malachite  and  azurite copper mineralization were observed in the biotite gneiss. The gneisses are coarse grained, composed majorly of quartz, feldspars and biotite. Copper mineralization in pegmatites are also a common occurrence in the area. The pegmatites vary in composition and texture but in general are  all  granitic,  coarse  grained  with  the  main  mineral  constituents being feldspars and quartz. Lastly, copper occurs in dykes which are medium  to  coarse  grained  with  a  general  composition  of  quartz, feldspars and biotite. The dykes occur both concordant and discordant to the biotite gneiss that host them.

The  Ministry  of  Mining,  Blue  Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs recently concluded a nationwide airborne geophysical survey and is in custody  of  the  latest  radiometric  and  magnetic  data  over  the  project area. The data and resultant grids form primary geophysical information for the winning bidder in undertaking detailed exploration over the area.

Project Location, Geological Setting and Estimates

Location:  The  project  is  situated  in  Tharaka  Nithi  County  within the  following  coordinates  0°03 ′ 12''N,  38°02 ′ 05''E  to  0°04 ′ 57''S, 38°09 ′ 50''E and covering an area of approximately 196.2800 km ² .

Geological Setting: Copper mineralization in this area is found in three forms namely: the biotite schists, pegmatites and within dykes. Both  malachite  and  azurite  copper  mineralization  are  found  in  the biotite  gneiss.  The  pegmatites  that  bear  copper  vary  in  composition and texture but in general are all granitic, coarse grained with the main mineral constituents being feldspars and quartz. Lastly, copper occur in dykes which  are medium  to  coarse grained with a general composition  of  quartz,  feldspars  and  biotite.  The  dykes  occur  both concordant and discordant to the biotite gneiss that host them.

Resource Estimates: XRF results has shown copper concentrations ranging from about 1-31% across the areas covering Kamacabi, Gatue, Kiamiramba and Maragwa. Additionally, AAS results from Maragwa showed a chalcopyrite copper ore with abundance ranging from 2.619.5%.  A  NW-SE  trending  low  mag  anomaly  approximately  200 meters long and 70 meters wide is observed in the far-right section of the area suspected to host the copper mineralization.

Accessibility:  The  area  is  accessible  through  Nairobi-Meru  Road and  branching  off  at  Embu-  Ishiara  road.  Meru  -  Marimanti  Road equally leads to the study area.

Coordinates

1 | 0° 3 ′ 12 ″ | N | 38° 02 ′ 05 ″ | E
2 | 0° 2 ′ 28 ″ | N | 38° 10 ′ 59 ″ | E
3 | 0° 4 ′ 57 ″ | S | 38° 09 ′ 50 ″ | E
4 | 0° 4 ′ 42 ″ | S | 38° 02 ′ 44 ″ | E

Invitation for Expression of Interest (EOI)

In exercise of the powers conferred by sections 14 (1) and 223 (2) ( e )  of  the  Mining  Act  (Cap.  306)  and  2017  Regulations;  award  of mineral rights by tender, the  Government  of  Kenya  is  inviting expressions of interest (EOI) from suitably qualified mining operators to commercialize the Kamacabi mineral deposits.

Qualifying Criteria

Firms expressing interest will be required to possess the following key qualifications:-

(i) Vast  experience  in  exploration  and  mining  for  specialty minerals such as copper in global jurisdictions.

(ii) Verifiable financial resources to undertake detailed exploration and mine development.

(iii) Skilled, experienced and proven technical team of experts in exploration and mining.

(iv) Experienced management  team with a track record of successfully executed similar projects.

(v) Robust corporate governance framework.

(vi) Portfolio  of  past  underground  and  surface  rock  engineering expertise.

(vii) Demonstrable execution of similar projects in fragile ecosystems.

(viii) Ability to design and commission  start to end on-site processing  and  beneficiation  plant:  Ability  to  process  the minerals locally and contribute significantly to global supply chains.

(ix) Commitment to sustainability practices, including the adoption and use of green and renewable energy.

(x) Environmental Responsibility: commitment to implementing measurable interventions to minimize environmental impact, such as land rehabilitation and water management.

(xi) Community Engagement: Working closely with local communities  to  ensure  social  and  economic  benefits  are shared.

(xii) Have  clear  understanding  of  Kenya  laws  on  free  carry interest, FCI and State involvement on strategic minerals.

(xiii) Membership  to  regional  or  global  group  organisations  that encourage equitable and responsible mining.

COST OF EXPRESSION OF INTEREST

Bidders are expected to fully acquaint themselves with the conditions, requirements and specifications of this EOI before submitting  responses.  Each  bidder  assumes  all  risks  for  resource commitment and expenses, direct or indirect, of EOI preparation and participation  throughout  the  EOI  process.  The  Ministry  will  not  be responsible directly or indirectly for any costs incurred by Companies in submitting their EOI.

Additional Terms and Conditions

Any information and/or documents supplied to the Ministry, at any time  before  this  request,  shall  not  be  considered  in  evaluating  this proposal, and consequently, companies shall not make any reference to such information and or documents in their response to this request.

An omission to disclose material information, a factual inaccuracy, and/or a misrepresentation of fact may result in the disqualification of a response, or cancellation of any subsequent award.

This  EOI  is  an  expression  of  interest  only  and  not  an  offer document; responses arising from this EOI must not be construed as acceptance of an offer or imply the existence of a contract between the parties. By submission of the EOI, Companies shall be deemed to have satisfied themselves with, and to have accepted all Terms  & Conditions of this EOI. The  Ministry makes  no  representation, warranty, assurance, guarantee or endorsements to any bidder concerning the EOI, whether with regard to its accuracy, completeness or otherwise and the Ministry shall have no liability towards bidding companies or any other party in connection therewith.

The envelopes should be marked as follows:-

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4261

THE MINING ACT

( Cap . 306)

THE MINING (AWARD OF MINERAL RIGHTS BY TENDER) REGULATIONS

( L.N. 153 of 2017)

TENDER NOTICE

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by regulation 6 (1) (a) of the Mining (Award of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017, the Cabinet Secretary for Mining, Blue Economy and Maritime Affairs advertises the following tender:-

REQUEST FOR EXPRESSION OF INTEREST FOR LARGE SCALE MINING RIGHTS FOR MANGANESE AT LALI HILLS TANA RIVER COUNTY, KENYA

Project Background

The Government of Kenya, through the Ministry of Mining, Blue Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs,  has  designated  several  minerals  as Strategic and Critical Minerals. Manganese is one such critical mineral that is important in the green energy transition. To commercialize this resource, the Government plans to award mineral rights over the area through  a  public  tender  process  in  accordance  with  the  Mining  Act (Cap.  306)  and  the  Mining  (Award  of  Mineral  Rights  by  Tender) Regulations, 2017.

Upon  issuance  of  the  Mineral  Right  (Prospecting  Licence),  the project proponent will be expected to adhere to the provisions of the Mining Act and its attendant regulations.

Project Overview

The Lali Hills  prospect  was  discovered  by  the  Kenya  Mines  and Geological Department in the 1950s. These geological investigations, including regional mapping of the Mid-Galana Area (Degree Sheet 66 NW)  and  studies  in  the  Lali  Hills-Dakadima  area,  documented  the presence  of  manganese  mineralization  associated  with  brecciated sandstone units within structural zones. However, little work was done owing to the remoteness of the area and also commodity prices.

Manganese has been mined in Kilifi County for a long time. The deposit  presents  itself  as  nodules  and  pebbles  whose  source  has  not been  established.  The  deposit  unconformably  overlies  coral  reefs, suggesting transport and deposition from a nearby fumarole.

Among KNAGS, the source of this manganese has been identified as Lali Hills.

Manganese  is  vital  and  irreplaceable  in  steelmaking,  and  a  few nations  dominate  the  global  mining  industry.  It  is  considered  one  of the  most  critical  minerals.  Manganese  plays  an  important  role  in battery  production,  especially  in  alkaline  and  lithium-ion  batteries. Manganese  dioxide  (MnO ₂ )  is  often  used  as  a  cathode  material  in alkaline batteries, while lithium manganese oxide (LiMn ₂ O ₄ )  is  used in lithium-ion batteries, particularly for electric vehicles and portable electronics.

Manganese compounds are used in a variety of chemical processes. For instance, potassium permanganate functions as an oxidizing agent in water treatment and as a biocide. Manganese oxides are also used in producing glass and ceramics, where they serve as colorants.

The  Ministry  of  Mining,  Blue  Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs recently concluded a nationwide airborne geophysical survey and is in custody  of  the  latest  radiometric  and  magnetic  data  over  the  project area. The data and resultant grids form primary geophysical information for the winning bidder in undertaking detailed exploration over the area.

Project Location, Geological Setting and Estimates

Location: The project is situated in Tana River County within the following  coordinates  02°55 ′ 00''S,  39°13 ′ 30''E  to  03°02 ′ 44''S, 39°20 ′ 30''E and covering an area of approximately 155.7749 km ²

Geological Setting: The area is underlain by Proterozoic basement rocks  of  the  Mozambique  Belt,  which  are  overlain  by  sedimentary formations  of  the  Duruma  Group,  representing  a  Karoo-equivalent sedimentary  sequence.  The  principal  lithological  unit  relevant  to  the manganese occurrence is the Mazeras Sandstone, described as coarsegrained,  arkosic,  and  locally  kaolinitic.  The  sandstone  is  permeable and  susceptible  to  weathering  processes.  Extensive  superficial  cover and  weathering  profiles  limit  continuous  exposure  of  fresh  bedrock, making structural interpretation partly inferential.

Resource Estimates: This is a greenfield prospect whose resource has not been estimated.

Accessibility:  Accessible  via  the  Mombasa-Tana  River  Highway. The  area  can  also  be  accessed  through  feeder  roads  in  Tsavo  East National Park, as well as from Kitui County.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4262

THE MINING ACT

( Cap . 306)

THE MINING (AWARD OF MINERAL RIGHTS BY TENDER) REGULATIONS

( L.N. 153 of 2017)

TENDER NOTICE

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by regulation 6 (1) ( a ) of the Mining (Award of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017, the Cabinet Secretary for Mining, Blue Economy and Maritime Affairs advertises the following tender:-

REQUEST FOR EXPRESSION OF INTEREST FOR LARGE SCALE MINING RIGHTS FOR COLTAN AND OTHER MINERALS AT KIRITIRI IN EMBU COUNTY, KENYA

Project Background

The Government of Kenya, through the Ministry of Mining, Blue Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs,  has  identified  several  minerals  as Strategic Minerals. Columbite and Tantalum, Coltan are some of the minerals  categorised  as  Strategic.  To  commercialise  these  resources, the  Government  intends  to  award  the  mineral  rights  over  the  area through  a  public  tender  process  in  accordance  with  the  Mining  Act (Cap.  306)  and  the  Mining  (Award  of  Mineral  Rights  by  Tender) Regulations, 2017.

Upon  issuance  of  the  Mineral  Right  (Prospecting  Licence),  the project proponent will be expected to adhere to the provisions of the Mining Act and its attendant regulations.

Project Overview

The search for strategic minerals like coltan; important for electronics,  aerospace,  and  high-tech  industries,  has  made  geological mapping  and  exploration      increasingly  important.  Columbite  and

tantalum make coltan ore and are important components in strengthening steel and enhancing its performance at low temperatures. Capacitors in electronics are made from coltan ore as well. With the growing  demand  for  these  minerals,  expanding  electronics  markets, advancements in aerospace, and the renewable energy sector, Kenya's recent  classification  of  coltan  as  a  strategic/energy  transition  mineral has made  it a key hub for exploration. This decision by the government  aims  to  boost  the  economy  and  position  Kenya  in  the global supply chain, reflecting a worldwide effort to find new sources of these minerals.

In an attempt to understand the distribution of this mineral in the area,  a  detailed  geological  study  and  exploration  in  the  KiritiriKiambere area, located in Mbeere South, Embu County was undertaken. The study aimed to analyze the geological characteristics, distribution patterns, and economic potential of coltan deposits in this region.  Through  this  exploration,  the  country  seeks  to  assess  the potential of Kenya's mineral wealth to contribute to the global supply chain.  offering valuable insights for future exploration strategies and market  positioning  amid  Kenya's  ambitious  endeavors  to  harness  its strategic mineral resources.

The  Ministry  of  Mining,  Blue  Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs recently completed a nationwide airborne geophysical survey and now holds  the  latest  radiometric  and  magnetic  data  over  the  project  area. The  data and resulting grids serve as the primary geophysical information for the winning bidder to conduct detailed exploration of the area.

Project Location, Geological Setting and Estimates

Location:  The  project  is  situated  in  Embu  County  within  the following coordinates 0°32 ′ 33.81''S, 37°44 ′ 30.59''E to 0°48 ′ 50.62''S,  37°44 ′ 30.59''E  and  covering  an  area  of  approximately 189.0500 km ² .

Geological Setting: The area is covered by mobile Neo-Proterozoic Mozambiquan  Belt,  characterized  by  the  widespread  presence  of plagioclase  amphibolites  and  hornblende  gneisses.  The  area  hosts  an assortment  of  calcareous  rocks,  gneisses,  and  schists,  which  have undergone  transformations  through  granitization.  Within  the  study area, columbite and tantalum are found together in pegmatite bodies, quartz veins and also as alluvial deposits in the stream sediments.

Resource Estimates: the current study was not sufficient to produce figures that would define a resource or a reserve; however, sufficient data exist to support the widespread occurrence of coltan in this area. This is further supported by continuous artisanal mining of coltan that has taken place in this area for a long time.

Accessibility: Kiritiri in Embu County is centrally placed. Accessible from capital Nairobi through Nairobi-Meru Road and also through Nairobi-Kitui Road through the Seven Forks Dams Road.

Firms expressing interest will be required to possess the following key qualifications:-

(i) Vast  experience  in  exploration  and  mining  for  specialty minerals such as coltan in global jurisdictions.

(ii) Verifiable financial resources to undertake detailed exploration and mine development.

(iii) Skilled, experienced and proven technical team of experts in exploration and mining.

(v) Robust corporate governance framework.

(vi) Portfolio  of  past  underground  and  surface  rock  engineering expertise.

(vii) Demonstrable execution of similar projects in fragile ecosystems.

(viii) Ability to design and commission  start to end on-site processing  and  beneficiation  plant:  Ability  to  process  the minerals locally and contribute significantly to global supply chains.

(ix) Commitment to sustainability practices, including the adoption and use of green and renewable energy.

(x) Environmental Responsibility: commitment to implementing measurable interventions to minimize environmental impact, such as land rehabilitation and water management.

(xi) Community Engagement: Working closely with local communities  to  ensure  social  and  economic  benefits  are shared.

(xiii) Membership  to  regional  or  global  group  organisations  that encourage equitable and responsible mining.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4263

THE MINING ACT

( Cap . 306)

THE MINING (AWARD OF MINERAL RIGHTS BY TENDER) REGULATIONS

( L.N. 153 of 2017)

TENDER NOTICE

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by regulation 6 (1) (a) of the Mining (Award of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017, the Cabinet Secretary for Mining, Blue Economy and Maritime Affairs advertises the following tender:-

REQUEST FOR EXPRESSION OF INTEREST FOR LARGE SCALE MINING RIGHTS FOR NIOBIUM, RARE EARTH ELEMENTS AND OTHER MINERALS AT THE MRIMA HILL IN KWALE COUNTY, KENYA

Project Background

The Government of Kenya, through the Ministry of Mining, Blue Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs,  has  designated  several  minerals  as Strategic  Minerals.  Niobium  and  Rare-Earth  Elements  (REE)  are among  the  minerals  classified  as  Strategic.  To  commercialize  these resources, the Government plans to award mineral rights over the area through  a  public  tender  process,  as  outlined  in  the  Mining  Act  (Cap 306), and the Mining (Award of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017.

Upon  issuance  of  the  Mineral  Right  (Prospecting  Licence),  the project proponent will be expected to adhere to the provisions of the Mining Act and its attendant regulations.

Project Overview

The Mrima Hill Niobium and Rare Earth prospect was discovered by the Kenyan Mines and Geological Department in the 1930s. A joint collaboration with Anglo American Corporation in the 1950s carried out a significant exploration campaign, including over 9,000 meters of test  shafts  and  more  than  3,000  meters  of  drilling.  This  exploration helped in characterizing the deposit. It is located in the coastal plains of Kenya, approximately 65 km southwest of Mombasa.

The  Kenyan  Government  has  confirmed  the  presence  of  five elements-niobium,  yttrium,  thorium,  strontium,  and  lanthanumdiscovered through a recent geological mapping exercise conducted in 2022.  However,  the  Government  has  not  prepared  an  economic viability report for the prospect.

Rare Earth Elements (REE) have recently assumed global significance.  They  are  critical  to  modern  high-strength  magnets  and constitute vital inputs for a growing range of mass consumer electronics and military high-precision applications.

REE will play a role in the global shift toward a low-carbon future. Strong demand for high-tech products, combined with rapid worldwide  industrialization  and  population  growth,  has  increased pressure on the availability of raw materials including REE.

Niobium-based  alloys  are  exceptional  at  meeting  the  challenges regarding  fire  resistance  and  seismic  requirements  of  modern  artistic construction, so demand for them in the construction industry is likely to  continue  growing.  The  increasing  demand  for  high-strength  and lightweight steel in oil and gas pipelines is likely to create opportunities in the future.

The  Ministry  of  Mining,  Blue  Economy,  and  Maritime  Affairs recently completed a nationwide airborne geophysical survey and now has the latest radiometric and magnetic data over the project area. This data and the resulting grids serve as primary geophysical information for the winning bidder to conduct detailed exploration in the area.

Project Location, Geological Setting and Estimates

Location: The  project  is  situated  in  Kwale  County  within  the following coordinates 4°27 ′ 45''S, 39°13 ′ 45''E to 4°30 ′ 15''S, 39°13 ′ 45''E and covering an area of approximately 31.9 Km ² .

Geological Setting: Cretaceous alkaline carbonatite intrusion within the Dzombo-Mrima-Kiruku igneous complex, rich in niobium (up to 1.41% Nb ₂ O ₅ ) and REE (up to 7.12% TREO).

Resource  Estimates: Indicated  resources  of  5.8  million  tonnes  at 1.41%  Nb ₂ O ₅ and  48.7  million  tonnes  at  4.4%  TREO;  inferred resources  of  17.5  million  tonnes  at  1.41%  Nb ₂ O ₅ and  110.7  million tonnes at 5.61% TREO (cut-off grades apply).

Accessibility: Accessible via the Mombasa-Lunga Lunga Highway, with terrain including the Coastal Uplands and Foot Plateau.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 4264

THE MINING ACT

( Cap . 306)

THE MINING (AWARD OF MINERAL RIGHTS BY TENDER) REGULATIONS

( L.N. 153 of 2017)

TENDER NOTICE

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by regulation 6 (1) ( a ) of the Mining (Award of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017, the Cabinet Secretary for Mining, Blue Economy and Maritime Affairs advertises the following tender:-

REQUEST FOR EXPRESSION OF INTEREST FOR LARGE SCALE MINERAL RIGHTS FOR CHROMITE AT KANG'URA IN SAMBURU COUNTY, KENYA

Project Background

The Government of Kenya, through the Ministry of Mining, Blue Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs,  has  identified  several  minerals  as Strategic  Minerals.  Chromite  is  one  of  the  minerals  categorised  as Strategic.  To  commercialise  this  resource,  the  government  plans  to award the mineral rights over the area through a public tender process as  guided  by  the  Mining  Act  (Cap  306),  and  the  Mining  (Award  of Mineral Rights by Tender) Regulations, 2017.

Upon  issuance  of  the  Mineral  Right  (Prospecting  Licence),  the project proponent will be expected to adhere to the provisions of the Mining Act and its attendant regulations.

Project Overview

Samburu County lies within two principal geological domains: the Neoproterozoic Mozambique Orogenic Belt and the Cenozoic volcanic sequences associated with the Rift Valley and adjacent plateau volcanism.  The  Mozambique  Belt  is  characterized  by  polyphase tectonism, regional metamorphism, and complex structural deformation producing a variety of high-grade metamorphic rocks and intrusions. In contrast, the younger Cenozoic volcanic formations are linked to  rifting,  mantle  upwelling,  and  magmatic  activity  associated with  the  development  of  the  Rift  Valley.  The  metamorphic  rocks  in Samburu can be classified into gneisses, amphibolites, augen gneisses, granites and pegmatites. Gneisses outcrops are typically small, weathered, and constrained to luggas and water channels. Hornblende is  abundant,  but  commonly  weathers  to  dark  brown,  forming  equigranular blades within the leucocratic quartz-feldspar matrix. Amphibolite  derived  from  the  mafic  igneous  material  is  closely associated  with  vermiculite  as  an  alteration  product.  These  rocks  are frequently interlayered with biotite gneiss, metaquartzite, granite gneiss, hornblende gneiss, and calc-silicate gneiss.

Sections  of  Baragoi  within  Samburu  County  represent  a  unique tectonic environment interpreted as an obduction zone, where fragments  of  the  oceanic  plate  have  been  thrust  onto  the  margins  of continental crust. The rocks associated with this tectonic setting form the ophiolite sequence, represented by ultramafic suites, amphibolites, and hornblende-plagioclase gneisses.

The  ophiolites  are  associated  with  psammites  and  semi-pelites metamorphosed  to  upper  amphibolite  facies  conditions  within  the Mozambique Belt sequence.

The  Ministry  of  Mining,  Blue  Economy  and  Maritime  Affairs recently concluded a nationwide airborne geophysical survey and is in custody of latest radiometric and magnetic data over the project area. The data and resultant grids form primary geophysical information for the winning bidder in undertaking detailed exploration over the area.

Project Location, Geological Setting and Estimates

Location:  The  project  is  situated  in  Baragoi,  Samburu  County within the following coordinates 1° 39' 52'' N, 36° 45' 00''E to 1° 33' 44''  N,  36°  49'  24''  E  and  covering  an  area  of  approximately 213.3263 km ² .

Geological  Setting:  Chromite  mineralization  occurs  as  discrete pods hosted within altered ultramafic rocks; medium-grained texture, acicular, and radiating crystals exhibiting a vitreous luster, consistent with serpentinized ultramafic assemblages. The emplacement of chromite pods appears to be structurally controlled, with mineralization localized along numerous planes of weakness interpreted  as  faults/shear  zones.  These  structures  are  likely  conduits for magmatic differentiation and remobilization, concentrating chromite within discrete zones, typically associated with dismembered ophiolitic ultramafic sequences.

Resource Estimates: Samples taken from Kangura before the initial mining  by  SimKan  Limited  which  stopped  a  while  back  indicated these assay results, MgO at 21%,7% and 8%, Fe2O3 at 16%,18% and 21%  and    Cr2O3  at  47%,  61%  and  54%  respectively  for  the  three

specimens.  The  area  also  has  a  significant  amount  of  nickel  as  was shown by export assay certificates.

Accessibility:  The  area  is  accessible  through  Nairobi-MaralalBaragoi Road. The area can  also be accessed through Nairobi-Moyale Road  branching  off  at  Archer's  Post  through  Wamba-BarsalingaBarsaloi-Baragoi Road.

Coordinates

1 | 1° 39' 52'' N | 36° 45' 00''E
2 | 1°39' 52'' N | 36° 48' 25'' E
3 | 1° 33' 44'' N | 36° 49' 24'' E
4 | 1° 33' 41'' N | 36° 45' 00'' E

THE JUDICIAL SERVICE ACT

( Cap. 8A)

LIST OF APPLICANTS AND SHORTLISTED CANDIDATES FOR THE POSITION OF JUDGE OF THE SUPREME COURT OF KENYA

A. APPLICANTS:

On 28th January, 2026, the Judicial Service Commission (JSC) advertised the position of Judge of the Supreme Court of Kenya and invited  applications  from  qualified  persons  wishing  to  be  considered for appointment to the position.

At  the  close  of  the  advertisement  on  17th  February,  2026,  a total  of  six  (6)  applications  were  received  as  indicated  in  Table  1 below:

Table 1: Applicants for the Position of Judge of the Supreme Court of Kenya:

Applicant Name
Lilian Wanjiku Wachira (Ms.)
Hon. Justice Joseph Kiplagat Sergon
Hon. Justice Warsame Abdulahi Mohammed
Hon. Justice Joseph Kipchumba Kigen Katwa
Hon. Justice Francis Kipruto Tuiyott
CS Anne Waceke Kiratu Makori (Ms.)

B. SHORTLISTED CANDIDATES:

Following  the  shortlisting  exercise,  it  is  notified  for  general information that JSC will interview the shortlisted candidates on 28th and  29th  April,  2026  at  the  JSC  Boardroom,  CBK  Pension  Towers, 12th Floor, Harambee Avenue, Nairobi.

The  list  of  shortlisted  candidates  and  the  specific  dates  and time of the interview are indicated in Table 2 below:

Table  2:  Interview  Schedule  for  the  position  of  Judge  of  the Supreme Court of Kenya:

Name of Candidate: | Day/Date of Interview | Time of Interview
CS Anne Waceke Kiratu Makori (Ms.) | Tuesday, 28th April, 2026 | 9.00 a.m.
Hon. Justice Joseph Kipchumba Kigen Katwa | Tuesday, 28th April, 2026 | 11.00 a.m
Hon. Justice Joseph Kiplagat Sergon | Tuesday, 28th April, 2026 | 2.00 p.m.
Hon. Justice Francis Kipruto Tuiyott | Wednesday, 29th April, 2026 | 9.00 a.m.
Hon. Justice Abdulahi Mohammed Warsame | Wednesday, 29th April, 2026 | 11.00 a.m.

Members  of  the  public are invited to avail in writing any information of interest in respect to any of the shortlisted candidates using the contacts below:

The Secretary, Judicial Service Commission, P.O. Box 40048 - 00100, Nairobi

E-mail: recruitment@jsc.go.ke

Telephone: 020 2739180

Commission Offices: CBK Pension Towers, 13th Floor, Harambee Avenue, Nairobi

Take note that the Commission may interview any member of the public  who  has  submitted  information  on  any  of  the  shortlisted candidates and such information shall be kept confidential.

THE  JUDICIAL  SERVICE  COMMISSION  IS  AN  EQUAL OPPORTUNITY EMPLOYER. PLEASE NOTE THAT JSC RECRUITMENT SERVICES ARE FREE OF CHARGE.

WINFRIDAH B. MOKAYA, Secretary, Judicial Service Commission.
